        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2068378719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8508156919308626983">Disclaimer :- I was provided this e-book for free in exchange for my honest review and feedback.<br/><br/>The summery provided for the book actually describes the first 20 pages, The beginning is rushed as we hurry to get the MC into the virtual world where the story really begins. <br/><br/>This is an issue as it creates plot holes that are addressed by the end of the book and makes it seem more like back peddling then anything else. <br/><br/>Although this is classified under (YA) the writing style makes it more suitable f</span>
  <span id="freeText8508156919308626983" style="display:none">Disclaimer :- I was provided this e-book for free in exchange for my honest review and feedback.<br /><br />The summery provided for the book actually describes the first 20 pages, The beginning is rushed as we hurry to get the MC into the virtual world where the story really begins. <br /><br />This is an issue as it creates plot holes that are addressed by the end of the book and makes it seem more like back peddling then anything else. <br /><br />Although this is classified under (YA) the writing style makes it more suitable for 12 - 14 year olds, everything is overly explained and repeated. The book would benefit from further proof reading and editing.<br /><br />The action scenes and dungeon crawling is well written, the characters are distinct and the play on names although simple put a smile on my face. <br /><br />I'd say this book is an ok intro into litrpg for younger readers, but not for adults.</span>

  <span id="freeText1253011715474239923" style="display:none">When it comes to LitRPGs, this is one of the best!<br />The Characters are compelling, believable, and fun. Even more, the Game world that the books portray would get any fan of such games chomping at the bit to log into the world. Even if such a game was merely a standard MMO like WoW or EverQuest, you still want to experience it, although all the while you would be envious of the characters in the book who get to jump in with full VR immersion.<br />I don't want to add any spoilers to the review (Don't you hate those!) but what I can say is that I'm reading the sequel right no and as I marathoned the first book in under 6 hrs, the sequel should be done shortly as well!<br />A definite must have for all the LitRPG fans out there!!!!<br /><br />~Doc</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18296368671277805069">TL;DR: Give this a read if you want a fun LitRPG.<br/><br/>Stuck in the Game really shines with its fun characters, colorful and diverse setting descriptions that aren't just the generic medieval fantasy, and a mystery plot that really leaves you wanting more. The dungeons are great fun with the way they work, but the real interesting thing is how each one simultaneously adds to Noah's development in the game as well as the overall mystery.<br/><br/>The only flaw I could find was that the ending chapter was a bit f</span>
  <span id="freeText18296368671277805069" style="display:none">TL;DR: Give this a read if you want a fun LitRPG.<br /><br />Stuck in the Game really shines with its fun characters, colorful and diverse setting descriptions that aren't just the generic medieval fantasy, and a mystery plot that really leaves you wanting more. The dungeons are great fun with the way they work, but the real interesting thing is how each one simultaneously adds to Noah's development in the game as well as the overall mystery.<br /><br />The only flaw I could find was that the ending chapter was a bit fast, but I've been told the second book makes up for it so I'm really looking forward to reading the sequel, which I've heard is already out! Yay!</span>

That being said, interwoven within the game itself is an engaging mystery and characters that become more developed and engaging as the pages turn. Alot of thought went into the game itself, and the life or death nature of the protag. Even more thought went into setting t</span>
  <span id="freeText2291728369365677628" style="display:none">If you're one of the players who does the whole tutorial and reads all of the NPC messages, you'll love this. The game mechanics were detailed and complete, sometimes too much so for my taste but GamerLit is hit or miss for me. That being said, interwoven within the game itself is an engaging mystery and characters that become more developed and engaging as the pages turn. Alot of thought went into the game itself, and the life or death nature of the protag. Even more thought went into setting the clues and reeling you along for a tension laced ride.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p0ZzWredTvf6tMRHNNCbrKK8nKT74wbtD3HZaLCm3h2KGqiDzfJA1OSjReWlz9/wTZHa7a7FJyJLKqFX7EfyNQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wM07linPHVwTjx+3zgz70uWHBUenK39TCpPTcjY4t9LtkeBPU6ATfw2YnhVfE7+OCqpDDvINXpxOyKtNatmb+g==')})
  }

Thousands of autonomous computer programs, or daemons, make our networked world possible, running constantly in the background of our lives, trafficking e-mail, transferring money, and monitoring power grids. For the most part, daemons are benign, but the same can\'t always be said for the people who design them. Matthew Sobol was a legendary computer game designer—the architect behind half-a-dozen popular online games. His premature death depressed both gamers and his company\'s stock price. But Sobol\'s fans aren\'t the only ones to note his passing. This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
